1 Academic Resources

1.1 Big Picture

1.1.1 Introduction

MOSTLY, together, these resources, constitute our tentative OS, and take precendence for us, over all else.

1.1.2 The Big Picture: Some Non Tech Resources

  • Taleb, Nassim Nicholas, INCERTO: Antifragile, the Black Swan, Fooled by Randomness, the Bed of Procrustes. Random House, 2016.
  • Taleb, Nassim Nicholas, Skin in the Game: Hidden Asymmetries in Daily Life. Penguin UK, 2018.
  • A. L. Barabasi, The Formula: The Universal Laws of Success. Little, Brown, 2018.
  • M. Mitchell, Complexity: A Guided Tour. Oxford University Press, 2009.
  • Boulton, Jean G., et al. Embracing Complexity: Strategic Perspectives for an Age of Turbulence. First Edition. Oxford University Press, 2015.
  • Bar-Yam, Yaneer. Making Things Work: Solving Complex Problems in a Complex World. NECSI, Knowledge Press, 2004.
  • S. Strogatz, Sync: The Emerging Science of Spontaneous Order. Penguin UK, 2004.
  • G. West, Scale: The Universal Laws of Life, Growth, and Death in Organisms, Cities, and Companies. Penguin, 2017.
  • Capra, Fritjof, and Pier Luigi Luisi. The Systems View of Life: A Unifying Vision. Cambridge University Press, 2016.

1.1.3 The Big Picture Nexus

  1. Introduction

    This document includes academic resources on some disciplines that, mostly, together, constitute our tentative 'Big Picture'.

  2. Mathematical, Computational Sciences

        1. General

      4. Artificial Intelligence
        1. Artificial Intelligence
          1. General
            1. AI: The Least Everyone Needs To Know
              • M. Mitchell, Artificial Intelligence: A Guide for Thinking Humans. Penguin UK, 2019.
                • The least everyone needs to know about AI. Additionally, to situate AI, Data Science, Big Data, etc. in the 'big picture', see, Scale by G. West.
              • P. Domingos, The Master Algorithm: How the Quest for the Ultimate Learning Machine Will Remake Our World. Penguin UK, 2015.
              • D. Auerbach, Bitwise: A Life in Code. Knopf Doubleday Publishing Group, 2018.
              • D. R. Hofstadter and D. C. Dennett, The Mind's I: Fantasies and Reflections on Self and Soul. Penguin Books, 1981.
                • A wonderful, enchanting book! One that got many all excited about everything in it. But, it is now dated and, by itself, quite misleading.
              • D. R. Hofstadter, Gödel, Escher, Bach: An Eternal Golden Braid. Penguin, 2000.
                • A wonderful, low tech book; though now dated, it is still excellent for learning some rudimentary theoretical computer science, AI, and much more!
              • AI Now Report 2018
          2. Complexity Science
            • M. Mitchell, “Why AI is Harder Than We Think,” arXiv:2104.12871 [cs], Apr. 2021, Accessed: Apr. 28, 2021. [Online]. Available: http://arxiv.org/abs/2104.12871.

    2. Software Development
      1. Big Picture

        These ought/can not be done linearly. Best done repeatedly with different amounts of emphasis on breadth, depth of study. It is better not to ignore these during early stages, however superficially attempted.

        1. General
          • C. Hanson and G. J. Sussman, Software Design for Flexibility: How to Avoid Programming Yourself into a Corner. Cambridge: The MIT Press, 2021.
          • D. Hoover and A. Oshineye, Apprenticeship Patterns: Guidance for the Aspiring Software Craftsman. O’Reilly Media, Inc., 2009.
          • G. Wilson and A. Oram, Beautiful Code: Leading Programmers Explain How They Think. O’Reilly Media, Inc., 2007.
          • K. Fogel, Producing Open Source Software: How to Run a Successful Free Software Project. O’Reilly Media, Inc., 2005.
          • “Software Freedom Conservancy.” Accessed April 9, 2021. https://sfconservancy.org/.
          • “Welcome - IEEE SA OPEN.” Accessed April 9, 2021. https://saopen.ieee.org/.
          • G. V. Neville-Neil, The Kollected Kode Vicious. Addison Wesley Professional, 2020.
          • F. P. B. Jr, The Mythical Man-Month, Anniversary Edition: Essays On Software Engineering. Pearson Education, 1995.
          • C. Fowler, The Passionate Programmer: Creating a Remarkable Career in Software Development., Pragmatic Bookshelf, 2009.
          • A. Hunt and D. Thomas, The Pragmatic Programmer: From Journeyman to Master. Addison-Wesley Professional, 1999.
            • A very nice, popular, big picture book for pro programmers. Not strictly required during the 80/20ing phase.
        2. Software Engineering
          • R. S. Pressman, Software Engineering: A Practitioner’s Approach. Palgrave Macmillan, 2005.
        3. Requirements
          • K. Wiegers and J. Beatty, Software Requirements. Pearson Education, 2013.
        4. Software Architecture
          • L. Bass, P. Clements, and R. Kazman, Software Architecture in Practice: Software Architect Practice. Addison-Wesley, 2012.
          • D. Spinellis and G. Gousios, Beautiful Architecture: Leading Thinkers Reveal the Hidden Beauty in Software Design. O’Reilly Media, Inc., 2009.
        5. SD Approaches
          1. Rapid Development
            • S. McConnell, Rapid Development, Microsoft Press, 1996.
          2. OOAD

            OOAD isn't just for Java programmers. OO ideas are ubiquitous amongst pro programmers. Knowing a bit about them is required for most techies.

            • The Object-Oriented Thought Process. Pearson Education India,
              • Understand rudimentary OO concepts without doing any/much coding
            • B. McLaughlin, G. Pollice, and D. West, Head First Object-Oriented Analysis and Design: A Brain Friendly Guide to OOA&D. O'Reilly Media, Inc., 2007.
              • Understand rudimentary OOAD.
            • G. Booch, Object Oriented Analysis & Design With Application. Pearson Education India, 2006.
          3. Design Patterns
            • E. Gamma, Design Patterns: Elements of Reusable Object-Oriented Software. Pearson Education India, 1995.

1.5.2 Communication Studies

  1. STEM and Languages
    1. Systems Sciences
      • “The Vermont Complex Systems Center,” Vermont Complex Systems Center at UVM. https://vermontcomplexsystems.org/index.html (accessed May 28, 2021).
  2. Linguistics
    1. Non Tech
      • T. Buzan, The Power of Verbal Intelligence. Thorsons, 2002.
      • D. Crystal, How Language Works. Penguin UK, 2007.
      • S. Pinker, The Language Instinct: How the Mind Creates Language. Penguin UK, 2003.
    2. Tech
      • A. Akmajian, R. A. Demer, A. K. Farmer, and R. M. Harnish, Linguistics: An Introduction to Language and Communication. MIT Press, 2001.
      • A. Radford, M. Atkinson, D. Britain, H. Clahsen, and A. Spencer, Linguistics: An Introduction. Cambridge University Press, 2009.
      • F. de Saussure, Course in General Linguistics. Columbia University Press, 2011.
  3. Languages
    1. English
      1. Grammar
        1. School
          • W. & Martin, High School English Grammar & Composition (Multicolour Edition). S. Chand Publishing, 2015.
        2. Miscellaneous
          • R. Quirk, A Comprehensive Grammar of the English Language. Pearson Education India, 2010.
          • S. Greenbaum, The Oxford English Grammar. Oxford University Press, 1996.
          • R. Carter and M. McCarthy, Cambridge Grammar of English Hardback with CD-ROM: A Comprehensive Guide. Cambridge University Press, 2006.
    2. French

      • V. R. Schwartz, Modern France: A Very Short Introduction. Oxford University Press, 2011.
    3. Sanskrit
      1. General

        • T. Egenes, Introduction to Sanskrit. Motilal Banarsidass Publishers, 1996.
      2. Miscellaneous
        • S. Pollock, The Language of the Gods in the World of Men: Sanskrit, Culture, and Power in Premodern India. University of California Press, 2006.
        • R. Malhotra, The Battle for Sanskrit: Is Sanskrit Political or Sacred, Oppressive or Liberating, Dead or Alive? Harper Collins, 2016.
    4. Hindi
      • R. Snell and S. Weightman, Complete Hindi with Two Audio CDs: A Teach Yourself Guide. McGraw-Hill Education, 2011.
      • R. S. McGregor, Outline of Hindi Grammar, with Exercises. Oxford University Press, 1995.

    5. Urdu
      • D. Matthews and K. Dalvi, Complete Urdu: A Teach Yourself Guide. Mcgraw-hill, 2011.
  4. Communication in STEM
    • “Communicating in Technical Organizations,” MIT OpenCourseWare. https://ocw.mit.edu/courses/comparative-media-studies-writing/21w-780-communicating-in-technical-organizations-spring-2005/ (accessed Jun. 19, 2021).
    • “Advanced Workshop in Writing for Science and Engineering (ELS),” MIT OpenCourseWare. https://ocw.mit.edu/courses/global-languages/21g-225-advanced-workshop-in-writing-for-science-and-engineering-els-spring-2016/ (accessed Jun. 19, 2021).
    • D. H. Foster, A Concise Guide to Communication in Science and Engineering. Oxford University Press, 2017.
